## Chronological information

### Timeline

[5 BBY](/wiki/5_BBY "5 BBY")[[11]](#cite_note-Kassa-11)–[1 BBY](/wiki/1_BBY "1 BBY")[[12]](#cite_note-Showcase_Date-12)

[[Source]](https://starwars.fandom.com/wiki/Template:TelevisionSeries)

:   "*Our world is exploding in different places right now, people's rights are disappearing, and* Andor *reflects that.* [In the show] *the Empire is taking over, and it feels like the same thing is happening in reality, too. I was impressed by Tony's social-realist intentions. He's created a whole new morality. It's very deep and humane—there is grief, mourning, hope, fear. It's not just primary colours here.*"
:   ―Fiona Shaw, in a 2022 interview on Tony Gilroy's *Andor*[[13]](#cite_note-Trumpian_world-13)

***Star Wars: Andor***, alternatively titled ***Andor*** and later marketed as ***Andor: A Star Wars Story*** for the second season, is an American [live-action](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Live-action "wikipedia:Live-action") [television series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Television_show "wikipedia:Television show") developed by [Lucasfilm](/wiki/Lucasfilm "Lucasfilm") and released on [Disney+](/wiki/Disney%2B "Disney+"). The series is a [spy](/wiki/Spy "Spy") thriller starring [Diego Luna](/wiki/Diego_Luna "Diego Luna"), reprising his role as [Cassian Andor](/wiki/Cassian_Jeron_Andor "Cassian Jeron Andor") from the [2016](/wiki/2016 "2016") film *[Rogue One: A Star Wars Story](/wiki/Rogue_One:_A_Star_Wars_Story "Rogue One: A Star Wars Story")*. The [first season](/wiki/Andor_Season_1 "Andor Season 1") premiered in [September](/wiki/September "September") [2022](/wiki/2022 "2022"), and the [second season](/wiki/Andor_Season_2 "Andor Season 2") premiered on [April 22](/wiki/April_22 "April 22"), [2025](/wiki/2025 "2025") with a new logo.

## Official description[]

*The* Andor *series will explore a new perspective from the* Star Wars *galaxy, focusing on Cassian Andor's journey to discover the difference he can make. The series brings forward the tale of the burgeoning rebellion against the Empire and how people and planets became involved. It's an era filled with danger, deception and intrigue where Cassian will embark on the path that is destined to turn him into a rebel hero.[[6]](#cite_note-Media_kit-6)*

## Development[]

#### Announcement[]

:   "*Going back to the* Star Wars *universe is very special for me. I have so many memories of the great work we did together and the relationships I made throughout the journey. We have a fantastic adventure ahead of us, and this new exciting format will give us the chance to explore this character more deeply.*"
:   ―Diego Luna, on reprising his role[[1]](#cite_note-Announcement-1)

Talks for a television series focused on [Cassian Jeron Andor](/wiki/Cassian_Jeron_Andor "Cassian Jeron Andor"), [Diego Luna](/wiki/Diego_Luna "Diego Luna")'s character from the [2016](/wiki/2016 "2016") [*Star Wars* Anthology](/wiki/Star_Wars_Anthology_Series "Star Wars Anthology Series") film *[Rogue One: A Star Wars Story](/wiki/Rogue_One:_A_Star_Wars_Story "Rogue One: A Star Wars Story")*, began before the Anthology film was released, though Luna had doubts that it would happen.[[14]](#cite_note-14) In [February](/wiki/February "February") [2018](/wiki/2018 "2018"), Disney CEO [Bob Iger](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bob_Iger "wikipedia:Bob Iger") revealed that "a few" *Star Wars* live-action series were in development for [Disney's streaming service](/wiki/Disney%2B "Disney+").[[15]](#cite_note-15) The series was officially announced by Iger during a Disney quarterly earnings call on [November 8](/wiki/November_8 "November 8"), 2018.[[1]](#cite_note-Announcement-1)

 [![A promotional banner for the series](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/f/f5/Andor_Promotional_Banner.png/revision/latest?cb=20201216211527) [![A promotional banner for the series](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/f/f5/Andor_Promotional_Banner.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20201216211527)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/f/f5/Andor_Promotional_Banner.png/revision/latest?cb=20201216211527) 

A promotional banner for the series

 

On [November 30](/wiki/November_30 "November 30"), it was reported that [*The Americans*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Americans_(2013_TV_series) "wikipedia:The Americans (2013 TV series)") executive producer [Stephen Schiff](/wiki/Stephen_Schiff "Stephen Schiff") was tapped to serve as a showrunner while [*Moana*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moana_(2016_film) "wikipedia:Moana (2016 film)") writer [Jared Bush](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jared_Bush "wikipedia:Jared Bush") was revealed to have originated the project by writing a pilot script and a [series bible](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bible_(screenwriting) "wikipedia:Bible (screenwriting)").[[16]](#cite_note-Schiff_&_Bush-16) According to [Production Weekly](https://www.productionweekly.com), the series was scheduled to begin production in October [2019](/wiki/2019 "2019").[[17]](#cite_note-Filming_Scheduled_Date-17) On [July 11](/wiki/July_11 "July 11"), 2019, [Rick Famuyiwa](/wiki/Rick_Famuyiwa "Rick Famuyiwa") was reported to be in talks to direct an undisclosed amount of episodes for the series, with filming scheduled to begin on [October 7](/wiki/October_7 "October 7").[[18]](#cite_note-18) On October 15, 2019, Variety reported that *Rogue One* co-writer [Tony Gilroy](/wiki/Tony_Gilroy "Tony Gilroy") would be writing the pilot for the series in addition to directing multiple episodes.[[19]](#cite_note-19)

Lucasfilm's original concept for the series focused on the adventures of Andor and his reprogrammed [KX-series security droid](/wiki/KX-series_security_droid "KX-series security droid"), [K-2SO](/wiki/K-2SO "K-2SO"), who is played by [Alan Tudyk](/wiki/Alan_Tudyk "Alan Tudyk"). The two would have a [Butch and Sundance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Butch_Cassidy_and_the_Sundance_Kid "wikipedia:Butch Cassidy and the Sundance Kid") style dynamic, with the two set to storm a citadel[[20]](#cite_note-Real_People-20) in the series pilot.[[21]](#cite_note-Controversial_Story-21) Thanks to his work on *Rogue One*, Gilroy was consulted for work on the prequel series.[[22]](#cite_note-TimesUnion-22) He thought the original pitch was "fine" but felt it was "very hard to sustain over a long haul,"[[20]](#cite_note-Real_People-20) questioning what they could do after storming a citadel at the show's very start. Furthermore, he knew from his experience on *Rogue One* that K-2SO was a hard character to work with for long periods of time, which would make an entire series starring the character difficult, lest Lucasfilm wanted to have to find ways to hide him during many missions.[[21]](#cite_note-Controversial_Story-21)

 [![Tony Gilroy's pitch for Andor took the character of Cassian Andor back five years and followed him into "the worst night of his life](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/2/2e/Andor1-Cassiankillsguard.png/revision/latest?cb=20240604013734) [![Tony Gilroy's pitch for Andor took the character of Cassian Andor back five years and followed him into "the worst night of his life](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/2/2e/Andor1-Cassiankillsguard.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/300?cb=20240604013734)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/2/2e/Andor1-Cassiankillsguard.png/revision/latest?cb=20240604013734) 

Tony Gilroy's pitch for *Andor* took the character of Cassian Andor back five years and followed him into "the worst night of his life."

 

Without outright saying he was interested, Gilroy responded with what was later called "a long forensic manifesto" to Lucasfilm, outlining his issues with the pitch and putting forth his own ideas. Gilroy's idea was the story that would become *Andor*,[[20]](#cite_note-Real_People-20) pitching a story that took Andor himself "back five years, to the worst night of his life." In the process, the series would see Andor evolve into the man first seen in *Rogue One*. According to Gilroy, Lucasfilm thought his pitch "looked a little insane,"[[22]](#cite_note-TimesUnion-22) and he fully admitted the story he had in mind was "a crazy idea" and "radical."[[20]](#cite_note-Real_People-20) In the end, however, Lucasfilm decided Gilroy's story was the route to go.[[22]](#cite_note-TimesUnion-22)

#### Gilroy's concepts[]

##### Overview[]

It is requested that this article section [be expanded](/wiki/Special:EditPage/:Star_Wars:_Andor "Special:EditPage/:Star Wars: Andor"). *Please improve it in any way that you see fit, and remove this notice once the article section is more complete.*

As far back as his pitch to Lucasfilm, Gilroy, as a student of history, wanted to imbue the series with themes of revolution, fascism, politics, rebellion, and the regular people caught up on those conflicts.[[22]](#cite_note-TimesUnion-22) When Gilroy was asked about political resonances in *Andor* in November 2022, he stated that the series was written without contemporary politics in mind, drawing on historical revolutions simply as spontaneous events to drive the characters' adventures—"whatever contemporary resonance it has is usually in the eye of the beholder. Oppression is oppression."[[23]](#cite_note-Oppression-23) In another November interview, Gilroy emphasized that his personal politics are "absolutely not important" to the series' themes and that *Star Wars* allows plentiful comparisons to history. As to the "age old question" of "who's a terrorist and who's a freedom fighter," Gilroy wanted every character to "speak for themselves" to make their motives believable and referred the idea of controversial revolutionaries to historical nation-building movements, naming the United States' [Thomas Jefferson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson "wikipedia:Thomas Jefferson") and South Africa [Nelson Mandela](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nelson_Mandela "wikipedia:Nelson Mandela") and further listing the revolutions of France, [Haiti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haiti "wikipedia:Haiti"), [Russia and the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/October_Revolution "wikipedia:October Revolution"), and the nation-building of Israel.[[24]](#cite_note-Themes-24) The [season one finale](/wiki/Rix_Road_(episode) "Rix Road (episode)") took inspiration from the 1966 [Gillo Pontecorvo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gillo_Pontecorvo "wikipedia:Gillo Pontecorvo") film [*The Battle of Algiers*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Battle_of_Algiers "wikipedia:The Battle of Algiers"), which was based on the [Algerian War of Independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algerian_War "wikipedia:Algerian War") against the colonial [French government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Fourth_Republic "wikipedia:French Fourth Republic").[[25]](#cite_note-Algiers-25)

Gilroy also likened *Andor*'s character of [Luthen Rael](/wiki/Luthen_Rael "Luthen Rael") as a [start-up company](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Startup_company "wikipedia:Startup company") founder[[24]](#cite_note-Themes-24) and, earlier in September, identified the senator and eventual Rebel Alliance leader [Mon Mothma](/wiki/Mon_Mothma "Mon Mothma") as a "figurehead of [liberal democracy](/wiki/Democracy "Democracy") that will fail"[[26]](#cite_note-Mothma-26)—he compared her to [US House Speaker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speaker_of_the_United_States_House_of_Representatives "wikipedia:Speaker of the United States House of Representatives") [Nancy Pelosi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nancy_Pelosi "wikipedia:Nancy Pelosi") in another interview in the same month.[[27]](#cite_note-Pelosi-27) [Fiona Shaw](/wiki/Fiona_Shaw "Fiona Shaw"), who played [Maarva Andor](/wiki/Maarva_Carassi_Andor "Maarva Carassi Andor") and spoke in an interview released in August 2022, thought that Gilroy's story is a "scurrilous" and "[social-realist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_realism "wikipedia:Social realism")" take on "the [Trumpian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump "wikipedia:Donald Trump") world" that was "exploding in different places right now" with people's rights being taken away.[[13]](#cite_note-Trumpian_world-13)

##### Five season plan[]

:   "*We were halfway through shooting season 1, coming through Covid, and the monumental size of the show, the effort, and everything else was just dawning on us. We realized that I didn't have enough calories to do it, and Diego's face couldn't take the timing, because it just takes too long to make it. We were saved by Disney saying, 'Okay, if you guys can figure out a way to do it, we're into it.*"
:   ―Tony Gilroy, on shifting to two seasons[[28]](#cite_note-Radar03-26-25-28)

Originally, Gilroy thought of *Andor* as a five season show[[21]](#cite_note-Controversial_Story-21) with around sixty episodes. It was during that planning phase that [Stellan Skarsgård](/wiki/Stellan_Skarsg%C3%A5rd "Stellan Skarsgård"), who plays Rael, joined the series, but he asked Gilroy to kill off his character at the end of season two so he did not have to stay for the entire series.[[29]](#cite_note-Vulture05-16-25-29) According to Gilroy, the five season *Andor* had the same overall story progression as the final series.[[21]](#cite_note-Controversial_Story-21) In the end, he would decide to pivot to just two seasons and believes that he did not lose anything major.[[30]](#cite_note-Backstory05-17-25-30) Gilroy reflected that he had only planned out season one by the time he was heading into a writer's room.[[21]](#cite_note-Controversial_Story-21)

As recalled by Gilroy, the decision to shift to only two seasons came halfway through season one production as the scale of the production became clear to himself and the crew.[[28]](#cite_note-Radar03-26-25-28) Luna feared that he would visibly age over the production of five seasons.[[31]](#cite_note-Popverse,_2024-07-24-31) Furthermore, Gilroy believed that there was not enough story left in *Andor* for twelve episodes across four more seasons.[[32]](#cite_note-Screenrant11-21-24-32) As a solution, *Andor* was shortened to two seasons, with the second season featuring four story arcs that each covered a year of the timeline up to *Rogue One*.[[31]](#cite_note-Popverse,_2024-07-24-31) In doing so, *Andor* fulfilled its purpose of telling a five year story. According to Gilroy, Luna and himself came to the decision together while drinking scotch.[[32]](#cite_note-Screenrant11-21-24-32) Luna, meanwhile, credits Gilroy for the "great idea."[[31]](#cite_note-Popverse,_2024-07-24-31) Gilroy considers season two "a fascinating experiment."[[28]](#cite_note-Radar03-26-25-28)

### Production[]

#### Season one filming[]

 [![The original series logo revealed in 2020](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d4/AndorSeries.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20220623213541) [![The original series logo revealed in 2020](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d4/AndorSeries.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20220623213541)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d4/AndorSeries.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20220623213541) 

The original series logo revealed in 2020

 

On [December 3](/wiki/December_3 "December 3"), 2020,[[33]](#cite_note-Kimmel_Schedule-33) Diego Luna confirmed that the series had started filming in London.[[34]](#cite_note-Jimmy_Kimmel-34) The title of *Andor*, as well as behind the scenes footage of the filming of the series, were unveiled on [December 10](/wiki/December_10 "December 10"), 2020 at a [Disney](/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company "The Walt Disney Company") investors meeting. Filming began in late [November](/wiki/November "November") of 2020.[[35]](#cite_note-Dec_10-35)[[36]](#cite_note-Sizzle-36) Although Alan Tudyk was initially announced to play K-2SO in the series,[[37]](#cite_note-D23-37) he later clarified in [January](/wiki/January "January") of [2021](/wiki/2021 "2021") that while production was underway, he was not going to appear in the first season. He did, however, expect to be brought into the fold in later seasons.[[38]](#cite_note-NoAlan-38)

The showrunners opted for practical environments, with scenes being shot at [Pinewood Studios](/wiki/Pinewood_Studios "Pinewood Studios") and on location. One scene was shot at [Pitlochry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pitlochry "wikipedia:Pitlochry"), [Scotland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scotland "wikipedia:Scotland"),[[39]](#cite_note-Empire-39) while exterior scenes for the [Aldhani dam](/wiki/Aldhani_dam "Aldhani dam") were also filmed in Scotland, at the [Cruachan pumped storage hydro plant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cruachan_Power_Station "wikipedia:Cruachan Power Station").[[40]](#cite_note-Instagram-dam-40) [Ferrix](/wiki/Ferrix "Ferrix") was very expensive to create. Gilroy stated its "mental build" took two years.[[41]](#cite_note-Perfect_Episode-41) Filming wrapped in [September](/wiki/September "September") 2021.[[42]](#cite_note-Diego_Luna_Andor_Details-42)

#### Season two production[]

##### Writers and Actors strikes[]

As part of the [2023 Writers Guild of America strike](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2023_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike "wikipedia:2023 Writers Guild of America strike"), Gilroy ceased all services on *Andor* and did not return to the set.[[43]](#cite_note-Gilroy_Ceases-43) A few weeks before season two's UK shoot was to finish, *[Deadline Hollywood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deadline_Hollywood "wikipedia:Deadline Hollywood")* opened an article by stating that filming on season two would pause as a result of the [2023 SAG-AFTRA actors strike](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2023_SAG-AFTRA_strike "wikipedia:2023 SAG-AFTRA strike"). Later in the piece, however, the article stated that, as per what *Deadline* had learned, the series was still being filmed at Pinewood Studios, but without actors who were part of SAG-AFTRA: American SAG-AFTRA actors had stopped work, as per the strike, while members of the [British Equity union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equity_(British_trade_union) "wikipedia:Equity (British trade union)") remained. According to the report, actors who were part of Equity were warned of potential legal action should they stop work in solidarity with the American union.[[44]](#cite_note-Filming_cuts_short-44)

##### Post-strikes[]

:   "*That's been our attitude all the way through: not to be cynical, and to take it more seriously than anybody ever took it. Even while we’re changing—some people feel as though it's changing a lot—but even while we're changing the grammar of what you can do, we’re trying very rigorously to be more serious about this shit than anybody ever has been.*"
:   ―Tony Gilroy, on making *Andor*[[45]](#cite_note-Gilroy_Gizmodo-45)

In [December](/wiki/December "December") 2023, [Kathryn Hunter](/wiki/Kathryn_Hunter "Kathryn Hunter") confirmed she would be returning as [Eedy Karn](/wiki/Eedy_Karn "Eedy Karn") for season two and shared some behind the scenes pictures via her Instagram page.[[46]](#cite_note-Eedy_is_back-46) She later took down the post.[[47]](#cite_note-Took_down-47) *Andor* was not present on [Disney+](/wiki/Disney%2B "Disney+")'s 2024 release schedule shown to the public in December 2023.[[48]](#cite_note-Games_Radar_S2-48) In an interview with IO9, *Andor* star [Stellan Skarsgård](/wiki/Stellan_Skarsg%C3%A5rd "Stellan Skarsgård") lit up with a smile upon a mention of *Andor* and promised he was satisfied with the ending, praising Gilroy's writing in specific.[[49]](#cite_note-Io9_S2-49) In a [February](/wiki/February "February") [2024](/wiki/2024 "2024") interview with GamesRadar+, Skarsgård stated season two would come in late 2024 or early [2025](/wiki/2025 "2025").[[48]](#cite_note-Games_Radar_S2-48)

### Seasons[]
